[Caraviello]: I spoke, I know I spoke on a Monday night and really tried to kind of tug at the sympathy and the respect of

[Caraviello]: the people that feel disenfranchised, and the reason why they feel disenfranchised, and please indulge me in a little bit of a history lesson, and I'm sure some of you know this, why the heck is a guy with the name McKillop even interested in this?

[Caraviello]: Well, my mom's maiden name is Joanne Camela Labasse, so I'm just as interested in what's going on as anyone else that's interested in this.

[Caraviello]: Columbus, it is something that is of historic significance for not just the name and not just the person,

[Caraviello]: but for the reason behind it.

[Caraviello]: Columbus is a word now that symbolizes something that's very important to the Italian-American community.

[Caraviello]: Columbus, back in the 1800s for Italian-Americans, was a person that did do a lot of discovery.

[Caraviello]: But in the late 1800s, 1890s, I don't know if a lot of you know this, but Italian-Americans were treated very poorly.

[Caraviello]: In fact, I would go as far as to say like dirt.

[Caraviello]: They were treated so poorly that there were certain Italian-Americans that were accused of a murder they did not commit and were acquitted.

[Caraviello]: And people didn't like that.

[Caraviello]: So they actually pulled these people, dragged these people out of a jail and they lynched them.

[Caraviello]: They lynched them.

[Caraviello]: They lynched Italian-Americans.

[Caraviello]: And this got so bad.

[Caraviello]: This got so bad in the United States that two countries were separating because of it.

[Caraviello]: the United States and Italy.

[Caraviello]: Dignitaries from Italy were removed from the United States.

[Caraviello]: Dignitaries from the United States were removed from Italy in the 1800s.

[Caraviello]: Imagine this situation and how it catapulted the Italian American community into a totally different level.

[Caraviello]: In 1891, the president of the United States recognized what was going on, recognized that this just cannot continue.

[Caraviello]: So he did something unprecedented in its time.

[Caraviello]: That's why it's 1,000, it's 1,000 something, 1,087.

[Caraviello]: Thank you.

[Caraviello]: Just if I could, just to clarify.

[Caraviello]: The city of Medford is not dictating where these 40B projects are gonna go.

[Caraviello]: What happens is because we don't meet the 10% threshold which is required by state statute, they're able to come in into 40B, which allows them to circumvent state law.

[Caraviello]: And that's what's happening right now.

[Caraviello]: So they can pop up and go anywhere they want in the community.

[Caraviello]: We're not picking particular sections for them to go in.

[Caraviello]: This is what is allowed under state statute 40B.

[Caraviello]: Thank you, Mr. President.

[Caraviello]: Thank you.

[Caraviello]: Marianne, are you finished?
